Hitler Clears the Fields and Prepares for a Decisive Battle with the Reds, The Finale of the National Socialist Party Congress, British Newspapers Call It Affectation

Nuremberg: The closing ceremony of the 8th National Socialist Party Congress was held today. Leader Hitler issued a warning to Soviet Russia, stating that if Soviet Russia incites a communist movement in Germany similar to that in Spain, Germany will have a decisive battle with it. We must admit that the communist elements outside Soviet Russia are indeed our mortal enemies. Hitler also stated that Germany believes that National Socialism is by no means an export commodity. Germany has its own political system, and other countries are free to choose their own political system. Hitler then sarcastically commented on the disasters in Soviet Russia, saying that the communists should not blame the famine on the climate. Pre-war Russia was abundant in agricultural products and the best in the world, but now it cannot feed its people. The flaws in its system are evident from this. (National Telegraph dispatch on the 14th)

Nuremberg: 17,000 infantry soldiers, many tanks, and several squadrons of aircraft conducted military exercises today as an embellishment for the closing of the 8th National Socialist Party Congress. German Leader Hitler and other National Socialist Party leaders, as well as diplomatic representatives and military attachés from various countries stationed in Germany, were present to watch. Hitler gave a brief speech to the troops on the spot, saying, "Serious times may be imminent, but we Germans will never retreat or cower." Hitler had given a final speech at the congress that morning, in which he launched an extremely fierce attack on Bolshevism, saying that Bolshevism is currently attempting to advance its troops near the German border. If it applies the methods it has used in Spain to Germany, we must treat it as one of the world's powers and deal with it. We Germans can remain calm, but if Germany feels threatened, the entire nation will rise up and drive out all the troops who think they can defeat Germany beyond the borders of Germany. Hitler also mentioned the Social Democratic Party's attempt to resist Bolshevism, and said that the National Socialist Party has now removed all of the above situations so that it can clear the fields and wage a final battle with Marxism. Hitler also said, "The countries of the world must eventually follow this path, and we dare to believe that no matter what country it is, it must make a decision for tomorrow as soon as possible. If people can respect us, they will find that Germany is the most loyal of their friends, but Bolsheviks must understand that the army of the new Germany has firmly guarded the gates of Germany." After Hitler finished his speech, cheers resounded throughout the venue. (Reuters dispatch on the 14th)

(London) The Manchester Guardian recently commented on the relations between Germany and Russia, saying, "The mutual verbal battles between the authorities of Germany and Russia are not without affectation. It is true that German Leader Hitler is very dissatisfied with Soviet Russia, but as far as we know here, he is also paying extraordinary attention to the current system in Soviet Russia. Moreover, whenever a real dispute occurs between Germany and Russia, the outside world rarely hears anything about it. Only this time, there was an open debate, so why wouldn't it be intentional? Didn't the Soviet authorities add serious charges against certain German officials on the day the anti-revolutionary case in Moscow opened? The seriousness of this matter was already at its extreme, but the German authorities ignored it, and the Soviet government did not lodge a serious protest with Germany, nor did it reveal the facts of the crime to the world. From this, we can see the extent of the mutual affectation." (Havas dispatch on the 15th)

Hitler Again Denounces Democracy and Communism, The Jewish People Protest to the League of Nations

Nuremberg: At 8:00 p.m. tonight, German Leader Hitler delivered his final speech at the annual National Socialist Party Congress, launching another fierce attack on democracy and the Soviet Union, saying, "Germany has always adhered to the principle of not offending others unless offended. Therefore, any foreign country does not need to worry too much about Germany's situation. We are not missionaries, and we will never spread our ideals beyond our borders, but we also do not want other countries to interfere in our internal affairs." Hitler then criticized the democratic system, saying, "We Germans have tasted the 'international fraternity' advocated by Western European democratic countries to the full in the fifteen years since the war. We absolutely do not care whether these democratic countries love or hate us. Although the former German democratic government received sympathy from various democratic countries, the German people today dare not accept this kind of sympathy, and it is only natural that these democratic countries will not sympathize with us, and it is also only natural that we should sympathize with authoritative countries. However, we always believe that the democratic system cannot create lasting countries." Hitler then attacked the Soviet Union, saying, "Before the National Socialist Party came to power, the Soviet Union conspired to infect Germany with communism, and we resisted it, so that Moscow could no longer interfere in Germany's affairs. For this reason, we had to recognize Bolshevism as a major enemy... Fortunately, the German people are very sensible. Even if Bolshevist Russia only wanted to lead the thinking of Germany, the Germans would regard it as a great shame. From this point of view, Moscow will always be Moscow, and Germany will always be Germany... A British journalist once asked me if Germany intended to split Europe into two major camps that confronted each other. I replied that this split was already a fact, because the people's front governments of several countries are cooperating with the Bolshevik Party and should be responsible for the split in Europe. These people's front governments probably think that taking a conciliatory attitude towards the Bolshevik Party can guard against the Bolsheviks. In fact, this is due to the indecisiveness of democratic politics. One day, the people of other countries may suddenly awaken and imitate what we have done. In short, what we admire most is Italy, because only Italy knows how to destroy Bolshevism. We also firmly believe that no matter what country in the world, it will eventually have to follow in the footsteps of Germany and Italy, because the purpose of communism is to destroy the whole world... I firmly believe that those who are superstitious about democratic politics will regard me as a 'savage'. In fact, I am better than most Europeans... We should now rise up, follow the instructions of God, and sacrifice everything to wish Germany long life." After the speech, the whole audience cheered, as if possessed. Hitler's voice was slightly hoarse when he spoke, but it did not diminish his enthusiasm. (Havas dispatch on the 14th)

(Berlin) German Leader Hitler recently gave a speech at the 8th Annual National Socialist Party Congress, announcing a four-year economic plan. According to this plan, all the raw materials needed by Germany will be completely self-sufficient after four years. It is now officially announced that the government will establish an "Academy of Applied Sciences," with the director of the National Highway Bureau, Todt, as its president. Although the specific tasks of the academy have not been announced, it is generally believed that this is the initial work to complete the policy of economic self-sufficiency. (Havas dispatch on the 15th)

After the Nuremberg National Socialist Party Congress was declared closed yesterday, Leader Hitler, accompanied by his entourage, returned to Berlin today. (Havas dispatch on the 15th)

(Geneva) The Executive Committee of the World Jewish Congress today submitted a note to the League of Nations, strongly protesting against the 8th National Socialist Party Congress in Germany "threatening and slandering the Jewish people," saying that it is appalling that this kind of movement is presided over by the highest authorities in Germany. The French Prime Minister Convenes a Labor-Management Conference to Discuss Ways to Eliminate Labor Unrest

(Paris) Prime Minister Léon Blum convened a joint meeting of labor union and employer representatives this afternoon, with the aim of seeking mutual agreement to prevent the occurrence of all future strike waves and to bring a swift end to labor disputes that hinder the general interests of the country. This joint meeting may last for a week. The meeting has also appointed six drafting committee members, including two government representatives, two employer representatives, and two employee representatives, to organize the drafting of an agreement between labor and management. (Havas dispatch on the 14th)

(Paris) The strike of 40,000 textile workers in Lille, demanding improved working conditions and increased wages, has been unsuccessful despite the Prime Minister Blum personally mediating. The situation is now becoming increasingly serious. It is reported that the employers' attitude is tough, so there is a possibility of a national general strike. Employers must now choose one of the following two paths: (1) Accept the government's suggestion of arbitration, which would involve signing a collective contract with the workers, stipulating a 40-hour work week and increasing wages; (2) Reject the government's suggestion of arbitration and be willing to have their industry eventually nationalized. They still have 24 hours to decide on their position. At the same time, the government has drafted an order to implement a 40-hour work week for miners, submitting it to the miners and mine owners for final approval. This is the first order on working hours since the government's proposal on June 21 advocated a 40-hour week becoming law. (Reuters dispatch on the 15th)

The textile strike in Lille has not yet been resolved. Employers have consistently refused the two demands of increasing wages and electing worker representatives. According to a letter from the employers to Prime Minister Léon Blum, "We cannot agree to the workers' demand for a wage increase, because this demand will bankrupt the entire textile industry. Also, the authority of the employer must be maintained within the factory." After a conversation with the chairman of the Textile Industry Association and the chairman of the Lille Chamber of Commerce, Thieriez, and the prefect of the Nord department, Cars, declared, "We refuse to submit to arbitration, and we do not want to sign a collective contract between labor and management, but negotiations have not yet broken down." At 8:30 p.m., Interior Minister Salengro issued a statement to the press, saying, "The government is scheduled to appoint an arbitrator tonight or tomorrow to resolve the Lille labor dispute." This arbitrator will probably be a government cabinet member, but it is still unknown whether the arbitration will take place in Paris or Lille. (Havas dispatch on the 14th)

(Paris) The Secretariat of the General Confederation of Labor recently held a meeting and passed a resolution to establish a "Support Committee for Striking Textile Workers," requesting workers in local unions to donate one hour's wages each week as living expenses for striking textile workers. The resolution of the conference stated, "Since the employers do not trust the government, the union should express its trust in the government and decided to send an important delegation of union representatives to visit Comrade Léon Blum to express sympathy and solidarity." Finally, the conference also decided to create an "Action Committee" with the freedom to act to resist the rumors and slanders of fascist groups. (Havas dispatch on the 14th)

Reuters Special Commercial Report on September 15

London gold price today is 137 shillings and 4 pence, down 1 pence.

US Dollar: The London foreign exchange market was stable but slightly choppy this morning. French Franc: The French franc opened with a rise of three pounds, at 76.87. At 11:00, it continued to rise four pounds, at 76.91, and did not change afterwards.

Securities

New York: The market was quite active this morning, but slightly choppy. The Republican Party's victory in the Maine election caused prices to rise, and the mood tended towards the bullish side. Stocks such as steel, railroads, automobiles, and steel mines were still being bought well. The rise in steel mine stock prices was due to the expected continued rise in domestic copper prices soon. Later, due to the influence of the election and the tension in the labor sector, selling suddenly increased, and prices fell back. Most stock prices fell below yesterday's closing prices. Public utility stocks and oil stocks felt great pressure, while automobile, railroad, and steel stocks traded well. By noon, general confidence seemed to have been restored, and the mood was quite stable. The New York market prices are listed on the left.

Cotton and Wheat

New York Cotton Market: There was a lack of interest this morning. General attention was focused on the October contract situation and the difference between near and far-term prices. Price fluctuations were extremely narrow. At noon, the December contract rose 1 pound to 12.07.

Liverpool Cotton: Today was loose. At 1:00 p.m., the October contract price was 6.56, 3 pounds lower than yesterday's closing price.

Chicago Wheat: The situation was quiet today. Negative foreign news and weak overseas market conditions caused prices to fall, but the market stabilized near noon. The December contract price was 110.75, 75 lower than yesterday. The grain market situation was the same as the wheat market.

Liverpool Wheat: Opening was quiet today due to disappointing overseas overnight news. Then, due to the expected rain in Argentina and good local sales, prices plummeted. At 11:00, the October contract fell 1 pence 625 to 7 shillings 6 pence 75.

Rubber

New York: The market was sluggish today, with narrow fluctuations. There was a lack of excitement this morning, and as a result, prices did not change much. Spanish Rebels Intensify Attacks on Madrid, the Capital; Northern Army Advances South Along the Coastline; Rebel Leader Announces Restoration

Andaye: After the Spanish rebels occupied San Sebastián, their morale has been greatly boosted. They are now preparing to advance south along the coastline with Bilbao as their destination. Residents of that city have already begun to evacuate. The American consul and his family, as well as other European and American expatriates, have departed. At the same time, the military operations of the rebels around Madrid have been intensifying daily. It is claimed that in the last three days, the capital has been bombed five times. The Chilean ambassador to Spain attempted to rescue women and children trapped in the Moorish Alcázar fortress in Toledo, but the rebel commander refused to negotiate directly, and the attempt failed. Although the Alcázar fortress has been repeatedly bombarded and mostly destroyed, the government forces still believe it must be captured before the rebels reach Toledo, otherwise Madrid may be in danger. (Reuters, 15th)

Burgos: General Mola, the commander-in-chief of the Nationalist Northern Army, delivered a public speech last night, stating, "What we demand is that Spain should hold an important position in Europe. After our victory, we do not want to be isolated internationally, nor do we want other countries to interfere. The only way to maintain national independence is to restore the traditional monarchy. In short, our goal is to build a unified, strong, and Catholic Spain. In addition, we should establish regional autonomy under a unified nation." (Havas, 15th)

Madrid: The attempt by the diplomatic corps representatives, Chilean Ambassador to Spain Mugardo and Romanian Commercial Counselor Ilfin, to rescue women and children from the Alcázar fortress yesterday failed because the garrison of the fortress used the excuse of wanting to seek instructions from the revolutionary government. After learning of this, the government forces immediately announced the termination of negotiations. (National Telegram, 14th)

Toledo: The Chilean ambassador to Spain, Magardo, came here the day before yesterday to mediate between the government forces and the rebels to rescue the women and children besieged in the Alcázar Palace. It is reported that the rebels in the palace have refused. (Havas, 14th)

San Juan de Luz: Following the intervention of Dr. Junod, a representative of the International Red Cross, the government authorities in San Sebastián have agreed to reopen negotiations on humanizing the civil war. However, the success of this effort depends on the Burgos rebel government agreeing to cooperate. (Reuters, 14th)

Madrid: This morning, government forces resumed bombing the Moorish Alcázar fortress. The garrison remained silent and did not return fire. It is reported that the garrison has rejected the mediation of the Chilean ambassador to Spain, Mr. Mourgardo, to rescue the women and children in the fortress. Mr. Mourgardo arrived in Toledo yesterday, intending to request the government forces to cease fire for a period of time so that the 600 women and children in the fortress could leave. (Reuters, 15th)

Castel Gandolfo: Pope Pius XI addressed 350 Spanish refugees today, praising the bravery of the Spanish clergy and the efforts of the diplomatic corps to humanize the war. The Pope said that although the goal of the diplomatic corps had not been achieved, their intention was commendable. The Pope mentioned, "The world has been threatened by reactionary propaganda, and the very foundation of the world has been shaken. The civil unrest in Spain has fully demonstrated to Europe and the world the extent to which the foundation of human culture is in danger." His emotions were so deep that he trembled slightly. It is said that when the Pope mentioned that certain people did not hesitate to create a new religion, it was generally understood to be referring to Germany. This important speech by the Pope was broadcast to countries around the world. (National Telegram, 14th)

Seville: The Nationalist radio station here recently broadcast a message stating that the Madrid government has decided to move to the southeastern coastal port of Valencia. (Havas, 15th)

San Sebastián: General Mola, commander of the rebel Northern Army, today ordered his troops to rest for five days, and then advance west to attack Bilbao. After the retreat of the government forces, they have now built machine gun positions in the vicinity of San Sebastián to await the rebel attack. The government forces' front line extends south from here to Achaibeheia, a strategically important position that is easy to defend and difficult to attack. With just a few machine guns, the rebel advance can be contained. The rebels will likely find future attacks quite difficult. (National Telegram, 14th)

Madrid: The fighting on the southeastern front of Talavera is currently advancing and retreating. The loss of this place would open a side of Madrid, allowing the rebels to drive straight in. General Asensio, the commander of the government forces in the central route, was ordered today to launch a counterattack to prevent the rebels from advancing. After fierce fighting, the government forces advanced six miles. (National Telegram, 14th)

Madrid: The roads in the capital and leading to the southern Talavera front are filled with crowds of people today. According to reliable sources, the government forces have achieved significant victories in that area this week. The cities north and northeast of Talavera have been recovered, and important positions south of Talavera have been captured. (National Telegram, 14th)

International Neutrality Committee Holds Second Meeting; Establishes Subcommittee to Handle Routine Matters

(London) The International Committee dealing with the non-intervention agreement in the Spanish Civil War held its second meeting today at the British Foreign Office. Portugal still had no representative present. The British government recently asked the Portuguese government why it was not cooperating with the committee, but has not yet received a reply. The Portuguese government is clearly sticking to its intended course. (Reuters, 14th)

(London) The International Committee for implementing the non-intervention agreement in the Spanish Civil War held its second meeting yesterday, deciding to form an informal subcommittee composed of representatives from Belgium, Britain, Czechoslovakia, France, Germany, Italy, Sweden, and the Soviet Union to assist the chairman in all matters. Representatives from a total of 26 countries attended yesterday, and the scope of the agreement was discussed. The representatives agreed to seek instructions from their respective governments as soon as possible on the issues raised. The resolution passed at the first meeting of the committee, which advocated that the proceedings of the meeting should be kept strictly confidential and that a communique agreed upon by the meeting should be issued at the end of each meeting, was reiterated at the meeting yesterday. It is also gratifying that most representatives have submitted reports outlining the legislative and administrative plans taken by their countries to implement the non-intervention agreement to the committee secretariat, and it is now planned to classify the submitted documents as soon as possible for the committee to consider. (Reuters, 15th)

(London) After its second meeting today, the International Coordinating Committee on Non-Intervention in Spain issued a communique stating only that representatives of most countries attending the meeting had submitted to the Coordinating Committee copies of the administrative measures promulgated by their respective governments regarding the implementation of the Non-Intervention Agreement in Spain. Furthermore, the Coordinating Committee's first meeting had passed a resolution stating that the discussions of the Committee should be kept strictly confidential, and this point is hereby reiterated. In addition, the Coordinating Committee has appointed an informal subcommittee with representatives from Belgium, Britain, Czechoslovakia, France, Italy, Germany, Sweden, and the Soviet Union as members to assist the Chairman of the Committee in handling day-to-day affairs. The subcommittee's first meeting is scheduled to be held at 4:00 PM tomorrow. (Havas, 14th)

Locarno Conference Unlikely This Month; Germany and Italy Await Clarification of European Situation

(London) It is confirmed that the Locarno Conference will not be held before November. German Chargé d'Affaires in Britain Bismarck sincerely stated during a meeting with British Foreign Minister Vansittart today that Germany hopes the conference can achieve good results and therefore needs to make full preparations. Russia was not mentioned in the conversation, but it was said that Germany hopes the conference will be limited to Britain, France, Germany, Italy, and Belgium at least at first. (Reuters, 15th)

(London) Informed sources believe that a five-nation conference of parties to the Locarno Pact could be convened in London in the third week of October. The British government is currently in contact with Rome and Berlin on this matter. However, the general impression is that both Italy and Germany feel that the date of the meeting is too pressing, and there is not enough time to make full preparations. It is also said that Italy believes that if issues such as the Abyssinian question cannot be definitively resolved and the situation of the Spanish civil war cannot be clarified, then it will be impossible to draft a detailed agenda for the Locarno Conference. As for Germany, it insists that the issues discussed at the Locarno Conference should be limited to matters related to the Rhine region. Britain and France believe that this German position is contradictory to the position Germany put forward at the London Conference in March of this year. At the London Conference, Germany proposed convening a conference of major powers to review Chancellor Hitler's "peace plan," which did include general European issues and was not limited to the Rhine region. (Havas, 14th)

(London) Various newspapers have recently commented on the upcoming Locarno Conference. Among them, the Evening Standard reported, "Regarding this matter, Italy, on the one hand, wants to reserve room for Germany's eastern neighboring countries to participate in the talks, and on the other hand, firmly stated that if the Soviet Union is allowed to participate, Italy will stay out of it." The Daily Herald reported, "If German Chancellor Hitler's speech yesterday afternoon was a solemn declaration of a carefully considered policy, then the future Locarno Conference will be in vain. In reality, Germany's diplomatic preparations are clearly intended to torpedo the Locarno Conference. If Germany is isolated, it is its own fault, so what is there to complain about?" (Havas, 15th)

Rumor States That Zuo Yi Dispatched Troops to Suppress, Situation Already Calm; Extremely Heavy Losses in Bikqi Village

(Beiping) After the establishment of the Suiyuan-Mongolian Political Council, the Mongolian Security Team in Bailingmiao was incorporated. The Second Company of the First Battalion, consisting of 900 men, was stationed with 500 in Chasuqi along the PingSui Railway and 400 in Bikqi. British Ship "The Lily" Suddenly Attacked by Farmers, Killing One Chinese Helmsman; British Consul-General Files Protest

(Hong Kong) The British ship "The Lily" was fired upon by farmers yesterday afternoon near Wangping in the West River, killing one Chinese helmsman and injuring the ship's owner, a Briton named Mr. Beyliss, the second engineer, a Belgian named Ramberger, and a Miss Kalette, a teacher of the American Church, who was a passenger. The farmers' actions were reportedly due to the ship's passage causing river water to flood their rice fields. Upon receiving this news, the British authorities dispatched the gunboat "West-Kuala" (625 tons) to the scene to conduct an investigation. Simultaneously, the British Consul-General in Guangzhou, Mr. Philip (who manages British interests in Guangdong and Guangxi, excluding Shantou), has submitted a strongly worded note to the Chinese authorities, requesting the immediate arrest and punishment of the perpetrators according to the law. The Chinese helmsman, who was in the wheelhouse at the time, died instantly after being hit by a bullet. Mr. Beyliss sustained a minor chest wound, Mr. Ramberger was shot in the thigh, and Miss Kalette was injured in the upper arm, fortunately not severely. Recent Missing Items from the Palace Museum Found to Be Re-emergence of Old Case

(Nanjing) Ma Heng speaks about the report that the Palace Museum has again experienced the theft of treasures. According to a telegram from the museum in Beiping, the counting of the Western Route Grain Depot on the 14th revealed the absence of seven sub-numbers within a large box. Upon investigation, the treasures within each sub-number were found to have been listed in the missing items list created in March 1928. It is clearly a re-emergence of previous missing items. These items were identified and verified on the spot by the staff of the related departments. The news report is, therefore, erroneous in this matter. The missing items list from 1928 contains over eighty items, and continued counting may reveal more. (Special dispatch from the 15th)

(Nanjing) Regarding the news report that the Palace Museum discovered the loss of ivory birds, etc., during the inspection of antiques on the 14th, according to a person from the Beijing Office of the Palace Museum, the Beijing Museum reported that seven sub-numbers were missing from box number 228 in the Qianliang Depot yesterday. Upon checking the list of missing items re-investigated in March 1928, totaling more than eighty items, all seven sub-numbers were included. The old record was shown to the temporary supervisors and police, and the true situation was explained to them. The cultural relics stored in the museum are now being recounted and registered under the supervision of personnel dispatched by the central government and local authorities, ensuring meticulous detail to establish credibility. The reported theft situation is, therefore, an old case discovered in 1928. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 15th)

(Beiping) Regarding the discovery of the theft of antiques on the 14th, the Palace Museum issued an official letter on the 15th, stating that the missing items were all recorded in the list of missing items from the reinvestigation of the Qianliang Depot theft case in 1928. However, among the stolen items in the old theft case, some were not included in the list because they had not been reinvestigated, and others had lost their identification tags due to changes in the displayed items. Therefore, there is no accurate statistic on the missing items, and missing items may be discovered at any time during subsequent counting. The counting over the years is a comprehensive inventory. The missing items in the Qianliang Depot, Silver Depot, and Cining Palace were all stolen before 1928, and they should be clearly verified soon. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 15th)

Regulations for Handling Election Lawsuits

Ordinary Criminal Procedure Applies to Election Crimes

(Nanjing) The National Election Headquarters has recently received inquiries from higher courts across the country regarding how to handle election lawsuits and election crimes. In addition to replying by telegram, the headquarters has also sent a letter to the Ministry of Judicial Administration, requesting that it be notified. The original letter states that election lawsuits should be governed by the Civil Procedure Law, except where the Election Law stipulates otherwise. As for election crimes, ordinary criminal procedure should be applied. The two have different natures and should not be confused. Please instruct all courts to take note of this. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 15th)

(Nanjing) The Election Office of Representative for Free Professional Groups previously sent a letter to the National Election Headquarters, stating that doubts had arisen regarding Articles 12, 6, and 14 of the implementation rules, based on reports from members of the Lawyers' Association regarding Chuan Kuanglin. The headquarters recently replied, stating (1) The Election Law and its implementation rules do not restrict the right to be elected for magistrates of counties, cities, townships, and villages, as well as personnel of various groups and organizations. Their participation in the election should be considered legitimate behavior. (2) As the implementation rules clearly stipulate in Article 6 that the ancestral home of the recommended person should be noted on the ballot, all elections should follow this regulation and note the ancestral home of the person being elected to be legitimate. However, whether the registered ancestral home is the actual or temporary residence, it is considered valid as long as it can accurately identify the person. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 15th)

(Nanjing) The National Election Headquarters has recently issued a circular to the chief supervisors of elections in each province and city, stating that Article 58 of the implementation rules of the Election Law, "Incumbent provincial, city, district, county, and village officials, judicial officers, and military and police officers shall not be elected as representatives to the National Assembly in the electoral district where they are located," is intended to prevent them from using their administrative powers to facilitate their election. The headquarters has decided that all administrative officials should resign from their positions before recommending candidates in order to participate in the election. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 15th)

(Xi'an) In the second re-election results of the preliminary election in Xijing City, Peng Zhenhuan, Wang Puhan, Li Zhiting, Hou Liangbi, Chen Guansan, Lan Guangbi, Yuan Youde, Wang Jiesan, Liu Chuyi, Hui Chunbo, and Yang Daqian were elected. Zhang Tingkuang and Tian Yi'an were elected from the industrial sector. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 15th)

Liu Wensong received 53 votes, Liu Guangfu received 23 votes, and Xu Fu received 22 votes. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 15th)

Cause of Derailment on YueHan Railway

(Hankou) According to the person in charge of the YueHan Railway Bureau, the derailment of the northbound No. 22 train near Yijiawan, Changsha, was caused by the fact that the highway line runs parallel to the railway line. The highway car drivers were reckless and actually raced with the train. Due to the strong wind generated by the passing train, the car driver accidentally allowed the entire car to be drawn under the water tank car at the rear of the engine. The water tank car jumped up, causing the engine to derail, and three third-class cars overturned in succession. The responsibility lies entirely with the highway bureau's driver's carelessness, which is very clear. If the car had temporarily stopped, it would not have been drawn in by the train. The YueHan train has resumed normal service, and the damaged cars are being repaired at the Xinhe engine factory. Follow-up matters will be handled after Ling Hongxun and Zhou Zhongqi return to the bureau. The first plenary meeting of the YueHan Railway after reunification is scheduled to be held in Guangzhou on the 18th. Chen Yanjiong is going south to Guangzhou to preside over this matter. Ling and Zhou are expected to return to Hubei at the end of September. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 15th)

Letter from the Secretariat of the Ministry of Communications

We have reviewed your newspaper's report on the 13th stating that Sino-British and Sino-American wireless telephone communications have been suspended, which is completely inconsistent with the facts. The Sino-British communications contract draft was initially drafted by our side and sent to the British side for revision, then sent back to our country and is currently under review. As for Sino-American communications, the contract draft was initially drafted by the American side and sent to our side for revision, then sent back to the United States. As soon as the American side agrees, we can begin signing the agreement. The report is prone to misrepresentation. Therefore, please make corrections to the report. Secretariat of the Ministry of Communications, September 14.

Shantou: The Evil Legacy of the Foreign Sugar Monopoly Remains; Smugglers Can Transport and Sell Sugar Unhindered; Chaozhou Merchants Who Report Taxes and Handle Sugar Are Detained Instead

Shantou Communication: Guangdong's sugar control and monopoly system has a provincially-run Special Products Monopoly Office in Shantou. All merchants must purchase sugar from the office. Each shop must sell several hundred bags per month. Only designated merchants can sell sugar. Small vendors selling sugar must obtain a license to store and sell sugar. Each market in the 15 counties of Chaozhou and Meizhou is limited to 500 sugar-selling licenses. The system was created by the former Director of Agriculture and Forestry, Feng Rui. This system is the most notorious example of harming farmers and businesses, and officials seizing profits from the people. "Five Rams" brand sugar is actually imported, low-quality goods. Guangdong's Bureau has been updated, the source has been cut off, and there is a shortage of white sugar in Chaozhou and Meizhou. The Guangdong-Hong Kong Sugar Merchants Association and agricultural and industrial groups accused Feng of ten major crimes. Feng was detained by the government and found guilty of corruption. He was executed by the provincial prosecutor on the 9th. However, there is no clear order to abolish the foreign sugar monopoly system created by Feng. It is now the Mid-Autumn Festival, and confectionery shops need white sugar to make goods for the market. It is impossible to find sugar everywhere, and the market price has risen to 26 or 27 yuan per 100 catties. The current market price of Hong Kong Java fine sugar is only 6 yuan 2 jiao per 100 catties. Therefore, smugglers are very active, repackaging foreign sugar into flour bags, each bag containing 50 catties, transporting it to the coastal areas of Hailufeng, turning to the interior of Chaozhou and Meizhou. Another route transports it to Macau, then to various parts of Guangzhou. The quantity is also huge. Chaozhou and Shantou merchants believe that since Shantou is under the control of the central government, all policies should be the same as in other provinces. Recently, they tried to import a batch of foreign sugar, paid taxes at the customs, and passed. Two days ago, the second batch arrived from Hong Kong, but after paying taxes at the customs, they were suddenly detained by the "Shantou Branch of the Provincial Special Products Management Office", accused of smuggling. The merchants argued that they had paid customs taxes, and the Department of Finance had not issued any order prohibiting merchants from importing sugar. Shantou is a commercial port under the central government, so how can it be called smuggling? The Provincial Special Products Branch ignored the merchants' reasons and detained the taxed sugar. The merchants refused to accept the loss and telegraphed various superiors, requesting the return of the original sugar to protect their capital. Since then, Chinese merchants have not dared to import white sugar. The Provincially-run Monopoly Office has no "Five Rams" sugar to sell, while smugglers are still importing large quantities of foreign sugar, mixing them with smuggled goods, and selling them at the current market price of 26 yuan per load in Shantou silver. After paying taxes, each load can still earn more than 5 yuan. Before the Mid-Autumn Festival, there is a huge demand for sugar everywhere, and it has become a business where smugglers monopolize the profits.

The Fujian Province is Establishing Agricultural Warehouses in Various Counties to Manage the Storage and Mortgage of Agricultural Products and Regulate Rural Finance

Fuzhou Correspondence: Since its establishment in the 24th year of the Republic of China, the Provincial Rural Cooperative Committee has organized over a thousand rural cooperatives in various counties, issuing loans of over 3 million yuan. It has also established rural daily necessities supply and transportation offices, borrowing 300,000 yuan from the Provincial Bank to purchase salt and kerosene, which are then transported to rural cooperatives in various counties for sale at reasonable prices, preventing merchants from exploiting farmers with high prices, greatly benefiting the farmers. Currently, to regulate rural finance, the committee plans to establish agricultural warehouses in the locations of various county district public offices to store and mortgage agricultural products. The committee will work with the three departments of Civil Affairs, Finance, and Construction, as well as the Farmers' Provincial Banks, to jointly establish a Provincial Agricultural Warehouse Management Committee. The number of committee members is set at seven. In addition to the ex officio members, namely the Director of the Civil Affairs Department, Gao Dengting; the Director of the Finance Department, Si Lie; the Director of the Construction Department, Chen Ticheng; the General Manager of the Provincial Rural Cooperative Committee, Xu Changling; the Manager of the Farmers' Bank, Shen Shuping; and the Manager of the Provincial Bank, Shou Changtian, there will be one additional committee member, who will be appointed by the Provincial Government. The Provincial Government will also designate one person to serve as the Chairman of the committee, presiding over the committee's affairs. A General Manager will be appointed to assist in handling the committee's affairs. The committee will be organized into four sections: General Affairs, Management, Finance, and Auditing, each with a director and three to four staff members and clerks. Each county will establish a County Agricultural Warehouse Management Committee with three to five members. In addition to the ex officio members, namely the County Magistrate, the resident instructor of the Rural Cooperative Committee in the county, and the heads of the offices of the Farmers' Provincial Banks, other members will be appointed by the county government from among the gentry and merchants upon the recommendation of the Provincial Rural Management Committee. The business of the Provincial Management Committee includes: (1) the design, registration, and management of rural warehouses throughout the province; (2) the investigation, supervision, and auditing of agricultural warehouses throughout the province; (3) the planning of funds for agricultural warehouses throughout the province; (4) the issuance and circulation of securities for agricultural warehouses throughout the province; (5) the regulation and supply of food grains throughout the province; and (6) other matters related to agricultural warehouses throughout the province. The business of the County Management Committee includes: (1) receiving agricultural products for storage; (2) receiving commissions from the Farmers' Bank to process, repackage, and sell agricultural products; and (3) other businesses specially approved by the Provincial Government upon submission by the committee. As for the storage and mortgage procedures, it is stipulated that the amount of the mortgage should not exceed 70% of the estimated market price when applying for storage and mortgage of agricultural products. The use of the mortgage funds is limited to the main production activities. The agricultural warehouse will collect the lowest possible interest on the mortgage amount as operating expenses. The rural agricultural product storage and mortgage fund and the agricultural warehouse construction funds have been agreed upon by the Rural Cooperative Committee and the Farmers' Provincial Banks to borrow 4 million yuan. A draft agreement for rural loans was signed on the 12th of this month, with an initial loan of 400,000 yuan as a mortgage fund for agricultural warehouses in Minhou County. It was also decided that for future loans, the Farmers' Bank will target the Rural Cooperative Committee as the borrower, with the Rural Cooperative Committee bearing the debt responsibility. The loan interest rate is set at 8% per month, stipulating: (1) Agricultural warehouses will provide mortgages based on 70% of the actual market price of the stored goods, and the agricultural products mortgaged in each warehouse should be used as collateral; (2) The storage period is limited to a maximum of ten months, from August of each year to May of the following year; (3) Each agricultural warehouse will have a director and a deputy director, who will be recommended and appointed by the Farmers' Bank. (September 12th)

Smuggling in Chaoshan is Gradually Being Suppressed; Customs' Anti-Smuggling Efforts are Strict, and Smuggled Goods are Gradually Decreasing; Smuggling Groups Disband; Chinese Merchants Refuse to Purchase Smuggled Goods

Shantou Correspondence: When Chen Jitang was in Guangdong the year before last, he heavily levied "miscellaneous taxes on imported agricultural products," formed his own land and water anti-smuggling teams, set up inspection and verification factories, and competed with the customs for priority in inspecting ships. Tax police and customs soldiers repeatedly caused misunderstandings and conflicts. From the customs to the Jardine Matheson wharf, they were both armed and on guard, almost forming a confrontational situation. This action not only became an international laughingstock but also provided smugglers with an excellent opportunity for smuggling. Central anti-smuggling ships could not be increased to strengthen anti-smuggling forces along the Chaoshan coast, fearing that minor incidents would lead to misunderstandings. Thus, the smuggling ships of Japanese ronin were able to roam freely in the waters of Nanao, Chenghai, and Raoping. They smuggled in goods subject to heavy taxes, such as foreign opium, self-refining products, alcohol, matches, Western medicine, silk cloth, and seafood, and simultaneously used armed escorts to export silver, tungsten ore, and other items. Rice was even unloaded in front of the customs, stored in warehouses, and transported to various counties for sale. The Guangdong land and water anti-smuggling soldiers dared not intervene. Sometimes, smuggled rice and beans intercepted in the inland rivers of Jieyang and Chaoan were also snatched away by armed ronin. The Guangdong authorities could do nothing. Fortunately, the Guangdong situation has now been renewed. The special tax on foreign rice collected by the Agricultural Products Bureau has been returned to the customs for collection. The land and water anti-smuggling Lanka Chen soldiers also voluntarily withdrew and disbanded on July 20th. The customs' anti-smuggling power was thus restored. Last month, the central anti-smuggling ship sailed to Nanao. The captain met with County Magistrate Lin Zhijian to inquire about the smugglers' smuggling and hiding of goods in detail and was trying to intercept them. Unexpectedly, the smuggling cargo ships were equipped with wireless telegraphs and were well-informed. Moreover, the engine power of these ships was very fast. Upon receiving information, they sailed to the Dongshan area, so it was impossible to capture them. Currently, Guangzhou has specially dispatched the Haiying, Haiwei, and Haiwu anti-smuggling ships to Shantou to serve. The salt police have increased by one company, totaling one battalion including the original one. The customs has added forty white-hat inspectors and one company of customs soldiers. The strength of the anti-smuggling force is stronger than before. The new anti-smuggling reward measures issued by the Ministry of Finance to Shantou stipulate that in addition to confiscating the smuggled goods, a fine and proceeds from the auction of the goods will be awarded to the informant at a rate of 50%. Many people are willing to act as informants. Customs officials have noticed that many goods sold in the market have not been reported to customs for inspection and verification but are flooding the market. For example, no one has declared taxes on foreign ginseng in the past three years, but the market is still flooded with it, with a continuous supply and very low prices. The same is true for fabrics and silk cloth. The customs had already received reports from informants and searched a foreign firm on Chaoan Street a few months ago. After being refused entry upstairs by ronin, they focused on Chinese merchant stores. A large amount of untaxed silk cloth was seized in various silk cloth shops in the city the day before yesterday. Even the stores' incoming and outgoing goods ledgers were taken away by the customs to thoroughly investigate the source. If there is no tax payment receipt proving the origin, date, and ship name of the goods, they will all be punished as smuggled goods. The investigation is currently underway. The Silk Cloth Trade Association, considering the strict laws and regulations of the authorities, specially resolved last night that all members of the industry should no longer sell smuggled goods. If this happens again, they will report it internally. Other trade associations are also willing to assist the government in anti-smuggling. According to investigations, the customs' seized smuggled goods are publicly auctioned once every Thursday. Previously, each auction would bring in more than 6,000 to 11,000 yuan (large batches are not included). In the past three or four weeks, this has been reduced by two-thirds, with each auction only selling for more than 1,000 yuan. This shows the decline of the smugglers' power. Smuggling groups have seen that the anti-smuggling power has been unified and that things are different from the past. Starting last month, they have stopped importing rice. The Tonghe Company, which handled rice in Hong Kong, was the first to close, and the combination company also closed last month.

Anhui Province is Actively Building Highways to Complete the Provincial Highway Network

Anqing Correspondence: The main and branch lines of the highways in southern Anhui have been largely completed, and all are equipped with bridges, culverts, and road surfaces. However, although the roadbeds of the roads in northern Anhui are roughly in place, the lack of stone materials means that most road surfaces have not been paved. The Construction Department has recently been rushing to repair roads, mostly in southern Anhui. This should be shifted to northern Anhui to achieve balanced development. The various roads that have already been started and the roads that are being added will all be completed as soon as possible. It is also planned to expand and renovate the roads that are already open to traffic, and to urge the counties to rush to build the county roads that need to be repaired, with the hope of completing the entire provincial highway network. The various roads that need to be repaired and built are described below: (1) The Jiangyu Road, from Jiangba in Mingguang, through Fuchang, to Yujiawa on the border of Jiangsu and Anhui, is 98 kilometers long in Anhui Province. The earthwork has been rushed to build in sections, and the bridge and culvert designs have started. All unfinished projects on the entire road should be completed by the end of this year. (2) The Chuliu Road, from Chuxian through Caishiying on the border of Jiangsu and Anhui to Liuhe in Jiangsu Province, is 25 kilometers long in Anhui Province. The roadbed earthwork has been completed, and the bridges and culverts have also started. All unfinished projects should be rushed to complete by the end of this year. (3) The Jiangming Road, from Jiangba in Mingguang, through the county seat of Mingguang to Mingguang, is 98 kilometers long. The roadbed earthwork has started to be rushed, and the bridges and culverts are being designed. All unfinished projects should be completed by the 25th year of the Republic of China. (4) The Quanpu Road, from Quanjiao to Jiangpu in Jiangsu Province, is 17.5 kilometers long in Anhui Province. The roadbed earthwork is largely completed, and the bridges and culverts are being rushed to repair. The unfinished projects should be completed by the end of this year. (5) The Hewu Road, from Hexian through Baidu Bridge to Yuxi on the opposite bank of Wuhu, is 30.5 kilometers long, connecting to the Xiliang branch line for 6 kilometers. The roadbed earthwork has been completed, and the bridges and culverts are being planned. The unfinished projects are planned to be completed by the 25th year of the Republic of China. (6) The Shenyin Road, from the ferry crossing on the opposite bank of the provincial capital to Yinjiahui, is 33 kilometers long. The formal bridges and culverts were completed long ago. Because the roadbed still needs to be raised, it is being rushed to repair. The road surface project is planned to be continued and completed in the 25th year of the Republic of China. (7) The Yintun Road, the section from Yinjiahui to Guichi, is 24 kilometers long. The roadbed and bridges and culverts were completed long ago. Because the roadbed is newly completed, the road surface has not been paved. It is planned to pave the road surface after the Shenyin Road roadbed is raised. (8) The Anjing Road, from the ferry crossing on the opposite bank of Anqing, through Dongliu, to Shimenya on the border of Jiangxi and Anhui, is 123 kilometers long. The roadbed bridges and culverts were completed long ago, but the road surface has not been paved. It is planned to continue to rush to complete it. (9) The Shuliu Road, from Shucheng to Liuan, its construction route, connects to the Anhe Road Taolin line to the Thirty Li Pu in Liuan, connecting to the Heliu Road line. The roadbed and simple bridges were completed long ago, and the formal bridges and culverts have been completed. From Taolin to the county seat of Liuan, it is 63 kilometers long, and the road surface is being constructed, and should be completed within this year. (10) The Chufeng Road, from Chuxian through Hongxinpu to Fengyang, is about 110 kilometers long. Recently, the county has decorated the earthwork to complete. The formal investigation of the bridges and culverts is occupied. After the investigation and reporting are approved, construction will start immediately. The unfinished projects are planned to be completed ahead of schedule within this year. (September 11th)

Suzhou Robbery Cases Occur Frequently

Recently, there has been an abundance of bandits and robbery cases in Suzhou. In addition to the four villages robbed in Weiting as reported yesterday, Lianmu Xiaxu Village and others have also experienced robberies and injuries. The incident occurred the night before yesterday. More than 20 bandits arrived by boat at Xiaxu Village, landed, and immediately fired shots to demonstrate their power. Under the command of one bandit, they divided into four groups and stormed into the homes of Village Chief Jin Yaoquan and villagers Hu Rongfu, Tian Shuanggen, and Tian Shuanghu, looting extensively. It is estimated that Jin's family lost clothing and other items worth over 200 yuan, and the losses of the other three families were also significant. After looting, the bandits boarded their boat and sailed to Guxiang圩 in the jurisdiction of Wucongjing. They then landed again and searched the home of the richest man in the village, Tian Zhaorong, and injured Tian's wife's leg and Tian's chin, robbing them of gold and silver jewelry worth about 600-700 yuan. At the same time, the home of Gao Zhengfei, the head of the Five Households in the Xihu Township of Xiangcheng Township, was also robbed by bandits at 1:00 AM on the same night (13th). Gao's wife, Gao, was also injured by the bandits, causing bleeding in her lower body. They then went to Fang Fuqi's house, and after robbing him, they took the loot and escaped towards Yangcheng Lake. The matter was reported to the security team and the Public Security Bureau yesterday, requesting immediate pursuit.

Chamber of Commerce Deliberates on New Tax Rates

The County Chamber of Commerce held a joint meeting of the executive and supervisory committees yesterday (15th), chaired by Fan Junbo on behalf of the chairman. Committee Member Yu proposed that the newly established business tax rates in Jiangsu Province place a heavier tax burden on daily necessities, and asked how to discuss and protest. It was decided that the Tax Rate Research Association and Committee Member Lu, along with seven others, should jointly review the matter and then make a reasonable appeal. At the same time, the Chamber of Commerce received a letter from the Bamboo Industry Association stating that the industry's 0.5% business tax rate was unsustainable, and requested that the association forward the letter to the Ministry of Finance, the Ministry of Industry, the Jiangsu Provincial Government, and the Department of Finance to reduce the industry's tax rate to 0.2% in order to alleviate commercial difficulties and benefit the people's livelihood.

Boat Collision Causes Tragedy

Xu Asi, the owner of a ferry boat near the Shuixian Temple outside the South Gate, had three passengers, Yin Meirong, Yin Asan, and Zhou Hejin, at around 7:00 PM the day before yesterday. They were crossing the river from Shangtang to Xiatang. As they were approaching the shore, they were violently struck by Zhu A'er and Zhu San'da's sugar boat and Song A'wu's Ningbo opera troupe boat. The passengers Yin Meirong and Yin Asan lost their footing and fell into the river. Yin Meirong was rescued, but Yin Asan tragically drowned. After the court appointed a prosecutor to conduct an examination, it was confirmed that he had fallen into the river and died. Song Awu, Jin Sijiu, and Zhu Sanda were all brought to the court for questioning. However, Zhu Sanda's brother, Zhu A'er, who was on the boat, suffered an acute stomach ailment. Upon suddenly seeing his brother cause such a disaster, he suffered a great shock, which led to his death. Yesterday, his elder brother, Zhu Arong, reported the death to the court for examination. Prosecutor Shen, along with officials, went to the countryside to conduct an examination, confirming that he had died of illness. The family members were ordered to prepare a coffin for burial.

The mud-carrying female workers repairing the Lianhu lock near Maqiao outside the North Gate of the county, totaling eleven people, were returning home after finishing work yesterday. They all boarded the ferry to cross the river. However, due to the small size of the boat and the large number of people, the boat suddenly sank in the middle of the river. Jiaxing Apprentice Bites Director

The Jiaxing Civilian Arts and Crafts Training Center is divided into civilian and vagrant sections. The training period for the vagrant section is mostly six months, and they can leave after the term expires. The director, Huang Tongsheng, believing that the center's operating expenses are limited, has been engaged in production to supplement the funds. Recently, he has added printing and button-making work. However, the working hours for the apprentices are over ten hours per day. Those who work hard after the expiration of the term are often deemed to have poor conduct and are subject to extension of their terms, which is not uncommon. As a result, the apprentices have accumulated deep resentment. On the morning of the 14th, apprentices Zheng Zirong, Wu Jinlan, Tao Ergong, Yu Yonggao, Tao Shaoguan, etc., surrounded Director Huang during the weekly memorial service and bit his back and left and right arms, causing numerous wounds. Guard Chen Rongqing was also struck in the head by the apprentices. The security team and police brigade arrived at the scene and arrested Zheng Zirong and the other four, who were detained by the Public Security Bureau for processing.

Bengbu Huai River Small Steamer Robbed

The Changhuai small steamers usually travel upstream. Only the Huashun and Futai small steamers travel downstream, between Wuhe and Linhuai, a journey of about 90 li. They depart in opposite directions once a day. The water surface is calm, and there are no bandits. Unexpectedly, a robbery of a small steamer occurred recently, which was unexpected. At 7:00 PM on the 12th, the Huashun small steamer, traveling from Wuhe to Linhuai, arrived at the Yama Temple, 12 li from Linhuai. Suddenly, more than 20 bandits who had been lying in ambush on the boat pulled out their pistols and forced the driver to stop. They then began to search the passengers, overturning boxes and chests. For about four hours, the passengers dared not speak up and let them loot everything. At 10:00 PM, the bandits landed and left. On the morning of the 13th, the Linhuai water police station heard the news and sent four boats to pick up the passengers and bring them to Linhuai. According to the victims, the Huashun was robbed, and the passengers' property losses were estimated at 4,000-5,000 yuan. However, no one was injured or kidnapped, which was a stroke of good luck in the misfortune.

Local News

Inspection Issues at Concessions Factories: The Consular Body's Opinions Have No Legal or Factual Basis; Secretary-General Yu Replies to the Shanghai Municipal Council, Hoping They Will Forward It to the Consular Body for Reconsideration

The issue of factory inspections in the Shanghai concessions has been discussed several times by Secretary-General Yu of the Shanghai Municipal Government and the concession authorities. A draft of nine articles was finally agreed upon in June of this year. It was approved by the Municipal Council board, which believed that factory inspections in the concessions would soon be implemented. Laborers were delighted. However, the Italian-led Consular Body in Shanghai expressed dissent and requested revisions, resulting in a de facto suspension of the draft agreement. It is now heard that the Municipal Government believes the Consular Body's opinions have no legal or factual basis. Secretary-General Yu has sent a letter to the Shanghai Municipal Council, hoping they will forward it to the Consular Body for reconsideration so that the original draft agreement can be resolved as soon as possible to ensure the safety of laborers. The original letter is excerpted below:

Regarding the case of factory inspections in the Special District, I received your president's letter of July 13, enclosing a letter from the senior consul to your bureau chairman, requesting review and reply. Upon review, the Consular Body's opinion is that the factory inspection agreement is "tantamount to partially abolishing the treaty privileges of countries enjoying consular jurisdiction." They advocate amending the draft to clearly stipulate that Chinese factory laws can only be applied to factories within the concession that are under Chinese legal jurisdiction. The enjoyment of consular jurisdiction by nationals of treaty countries cannot restrict the exercise of China's administrative power. The factory law is an administrative regulation, and the implementation of factory inspections is an exercise of China's national administrative power. Judging by legal principles and treaties, even those enjoying consular jurisdiction have no reason to protest. Furthermore, in fact, foreign-owned factories have often handled labor disputes in accordance with China's Labor Dispute Resolution Law. This is a precedent for foreigners applying Chinese law. Therefore, regarding the point of consular jurisdiction, the misunderstanding is already very obvious. As for the statement in the final paragraph of the original letter, "Alternative inspection methods can be established based on the powers granted by the Yangjingbang Regulations," regarding the essence of those regulations, the provisions for the existing administrative powers of the Municipal Council are all enumerated, not generalized, and cannot be arbitrarily expanded. Therefore, this government believes that the Consular Body's opinions have no legal or factual basis. Furthermore, I, the Secretary-General, was previously ordered to agree on a draft with your president, which took into account both legal principles and facts, and the positions of both parties have been carefully considered. The seventh article of the draft provides considerable remedies for the concerns of the Consular Body. This is what I, the Secretary-General, should urge you to pay attention to. I am replying accordingly, hoping you will review it and promptly forward it to the Consular Body for reconsideration so that the draft agreement can be resolved as soon as possible to ensure the safety of laborers. I also hope to receive a reply. Addressed to: President Fessenden of the Shanghai Municipal Council.

The Songhu Garrison Command Announces Temporary Partial Martial Law in the City from the 17th to the 20th of This Month

Since the Chengdu-Beihai incident occurred in this city, party, government, and military authorities have been making every effort to maintain public order, and it has not been affected in any way. However, reactionary elements hiding in this city are secretly active, sparing no effort. As the anniversary of the September 18th Incident approaches, it is heard that they will take advantage of the commemorative events held by various groups in the city, infiltrate those groups, and carry out large-scale disturbances. Yang, the commander of the Songhu Garrison Command, in order to maintain public order, consulted with Mayor Wu and submitted a request to the central government, which approved the declaration of temporary partial martial law in the city from the 17th to the 20th of this month. The Garrison Command's announcement is recorded below. Songhu Garrison Command Announcement: It is announced that, according to repeated confidential reports, reactionary elements are planning to secretly infiltrate various groups in Shanghai before and after the anniversary of the September 18th Incident, taking the opportunity to create disturbances in order to achieve their conspiracy to undermine the country. If strict precautions are not taken, unexpected events may occur at any time. In order to maintain social order and city security, this commander, with approval, will follow the martial law and declare temporary partial martial law in Shanghai from the 17th to the 20th of this month. During the period of martial law, gatherings, parades, strikes, class boycotts, distribution of leaflets, and any actions that may affect public order are strictly prohibited. Those who dare to violate these orders will be severely punished in accordance with martial law. In addition to separate reports and orders, this announcement is hereby made to inform all concerned. This is of utmost importance. This announcement is made on September 15th of the 25th year of the Republic of China. Commander Yang Hu.

The Banking Association: Representatives Sent to Beijing to Petition for Postponement of Income Tax Collection

Xinsheng News Agency reports that the second category of income tax, "income from securities and deposits, including interest from public bonds, corporate bonds, stocks, and deposits," will be taxed at a rate of 50 per mille, starting on October 1st. The banking and financial industries are requesting a postponement until January 1st of next year, to coincide with the collection of other income taxes. They have also dispatched Zhang Peishen and Wang Zhixin to Beijing to petition and present their views. The details are as follows:

Banking Petition

The Banking Association agrees in principle with the collection of income tax on securities and deposits. In addition to commissioning the Banking Institute to study specific collection methods, they request the Ministry of Finance to implement it simultaneously with other income taxes on January 1st of next year, as preparations cannot be completed by October 1st. They have already dispatched executive committee members Zhang Peishen and Wang Zhixin to Beijing the night before last to petition Gao Bingfang, director of the Central Direct Tax Preparation Office, and Liang Hejun, deputy director, and to present their views. At the same time, the association will submit its views to the Ministry of Finance for adoption. The petition has been drafted and sent to the standing committee members for signature. It is expected to be submitted today.

Financial Industry Study

The Financial Industry Association also agrees in principle with the collection of income tax on securities and deposits. After study by the executive committee members, they believe that it is necessary to solicit opinions from the members of various firms. Therefore, it has been submitted to the executive committee for decision and sent to various firms to solicit opinions, with a deadline of one week for collection in order to handle it. The deadline was yesterday, and opinions on income tax have been received from some member firms. It has been decided to submit it to the autumn managers' meeting on the 19th for discussion. However, the opinions of the firms are similar to those of the banks, and they all hope to postpone the tax collection until New Year's Day next year to implement it simultaneously with other income taxes.

Baoshan Seawall Protection Committee Telegrams the Provincial Government Requesting Appropriation for Repair; A Line of Remaining Dikes Nearly Collapsed; Terrible Winds and Giant Waves Create Dangerous Situations

A telegram from the Baoshan Seawall Protection Committee reads: Chairman Chen of the Zhenjiang Provincial Government, Director Shen of the Construction Department, Magistrate Zhang of this county, and all respected sirs: This month, a hurricane passed through, and the tide was high. The Baoshan seawall, a line of remaining dikes, nearly collapsed. Fortunately, the wind direction changed, and a major disaster was averted. However, the outer wing walls of Beishidong were completely destroyed, and the concrete wall of Beiwang Temple, 340 zhang long, has a hollow bottom and is leaning outward. Furthermore, the 42 zhang slope of the Chuchengjing section, which was repaired in the 22nd year, is almost completely gone. Previously, there were rows of piles to protect the outside of the dike, but they have not been repaired for many years, so the slope and the base of the dike are easily damaged. Other sections also have sunken surfaces and numerous cracks. Now, it is the season of autumn floods and high tides. If there are more terrible winds and giant waves, the situation will become unmanageable. People are panicked. Considering that the seawall project is of great importance, if there is any negligence, not only will the lives and homes of the people along the dike be lost, but also the land taxes of Jiangsu and Songjiang and the prosperity of Shanghai will lose their guarantee. We earnestly request that you quickly dispatch personnel to inspect and allocate funds for construction as soon as possible to eliminate the major disaster and bring lasting peace. We await your urgent orders. Zhang Jia'ao, chairman of the Baoshan County Seawall Protection Committee, Tao Qingfeng, vice-chairman, Gu Hongru, chairman of the Water Conservancy Committee, Bao Siren, director of the Public Funds and Properties Management Office, Wang Cheng, vice-director, Xu Liangxi, Lu Fengpu, Gu Xi, Wang Qingtao, Shen Buyin, and other district chiefs respectfully submit this document.

Guangdong Abolished the Night Navigation Import Ban; Shanghai Shipping Companies Celebrate the Notification

Merchant ships sailing from Shanghai to Guangdong, regardless of Chinese or foreign nationality, have not been allowed to enter Guangzhou at night since the 12th year of the Republic of China. They could only stay outside the port and be allowed to enter the port after inspection the next morning. During Chen Jitang's administration, the ban was strictly enforced, causing unbearable suffering to shipping companies. Regularly scheduled ships that needed to meet deadlines were often delayed due to the delayed entry into the port, causing them to miss their schedules. British companies such as Jardine Matheson and Butterfield & Swire have repeatedly negotiated with Chen Jitang

Striving hard, but they were unable to abolish this restriction. Therefore, for the past 13 years, merchant ships have not been allowed to enter the port at night, from sunset to sunrise, in Guangzhou. Since the central government unified the two Guangdong provinces and Chen Jitang fled, everything has been taken over by the central government. Wu Shude, the director of the Seaport Quarantine Office, personally went to Guangdong to take over the seaport quarantine affairs and fundamentally eliminated all the previous harsh restrictions, aiming to align them with the methods of seaports throughout the country. All bans on merchant ships

Night Navigation Import

were also deemed unreasonable and only caused hardship for shipping companies. Wu decided to abolish this ban on September 6th. Except for ships from epidemic ports, which must comply with quarantine regulations and not enter the port at night when arriving in Guangdong, but stay outside the port and wait for medical inspection, any Chinese or foreign merchant ships from any port can freely enter when arriving in Guangdong, no matter what time of night. The Guangdong Customs and the Seaport Quarantine Office have jointly announced this, and the official notification to Shanghai shipping companies was received yesterday. All Chinese and foreign shipping companies in this port were overjoyed upon hearing the news. From now on, ships traveling to and from Guangdong will not only save time for passengers and cargo, but also regular scheduled ships will be able to avoid past delays and missed schedules, saving a great deal on fuel and supplies. This is even more important now that the South China shipping industry is developing rapidly. There are 22 to 24 scheduled ships sailing from Shanghai to Guangdong, and many more unscheduled ships. Shipping companies have already notified all shipowners to take note.

Guangdong Public Bonds to Be Issued Next Month; RMB 6 Million in Loans Secured with Mortgages to Shanghai Banks Fully Disbursed Yesterday; Contract Signed for Continued RMB 2 Million Loan

Xinsheng News Agency reports that the RMB 120 million Guangdong Financial Consolidation Public Bond of the 25th year of the Republic of China will be issued on October 1st. Special Envoy and Finance Director of Guangdong, Song Ziliang, plans to mortgage a portion to the Bank of China, the Central Bank, and the Bank of Communications. The previous RMB 6 million has been cleared, and the contract for the continued RMB 2 million loan has been signed. Details are as follows:

Negotiating Public Bond Mortgage Matters

The RMB 120 million Guangdong Financial Consolidation Public Bond is intended to be used to supplement the preparation of silver dollar notes and will be issued on October 1st. The annual interest rate is 4%, the term is 30 years, and the funds for principal and interest repayment will be allocated from the unified tax revenues of the Guangdong region and managed by the Central Bank. The denominations are divided into four types: RMB 10, RMB 100, RMB 1,000, and RMB 10,000. Now, Special Envoy Song plans to mortgage a small portion of the financial consolidation public bonds to the Bank of China, the Central Bank, the Bank of Communications, and the China Bank to obtain cash as a means of consolidating Guangdong Province's finances. It has been decided to negotiate and sign a contract for the mortgage loan after the new public bonds are issued.

Previous Loan Directly Disbursed

At the end of July, Special Envoy Song borrowed RMB 6 million from the Bank of China, the Central Bank, and the Bank of Communications to consolidate Guangdong Province's finances, using the province's tax revenue as collateral. After the contract was signed, the loan was disbursed in four installments, each RMB 1.5 million. The fourth installment was fully disbursed yesterday by the Guangzhou branches of the three banks. He has also borrowed RMB 2 million from eight banks, including the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, the Zhongnan Bank, the Jincheng Bank, the Salt Bank, the Guohua Bank, the Dongya Bank, and the Guohuo Bank, using the province's tobacco and alcohol stamp tax as collateral. The contract was signed yesterday in Guangzhou, with a term of one year and an interest rate of 7.5%. The funds will be directly disbursed by the Guangzhou branches of each bank.
